URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS455734994	2018-08-04 09:46:27	6340	spuh	Larus sp.	Larus sp.			1				United States	US	Nevada	US-NV	Clark	US-NV-003	US-NV_982	33			Lake Mead NRA--Hemenway Harbor	L866915	H	36.0289024	-114.7754145	2017-01-07	11:39:00	obsr340220	S33527933	Stationary	P21	EBIRD	45			1	1		1	1	0			First noticed two large gulls in the expected group of California and Ring-billed Gulls. Both stood out instantly as much larger than the individuals of these two species. After more examination, I began to identify the smaller of the two large gulls as a second cycle Herring Gull. It has a yellow iris, a long thin bill, blackish primaries, pink legs, and some light gray mantle feathers coming in. It was also slightly larger than the nearby California Gulls. The other large gull, however, was noticeably larger and much stockier than the Herring Gull. The size difference is very apparent in some of the photos. I first played with Western Gull, but even that species is roughly the same size or even smaller than Herring Gulls. And the pattern of the primaries seemed not right for Western. This bird seemed much larger, bulkier, with short legs. The bird is obviously a first-cycle bird with its overall brown plumage. The tertials and primaries are much darker than the coverts and scapulars, but are definitely not black. The primaries show the faint white crescents at the tips when folded. The scapulars, coverts and tertials are all messy without any hint on organized checkering or barring. The inner greater coverts are based with a solid darker panel while the outer greater coverts are more mottled with white marbling. The median coverts show a white string of dots along the terminal ends. The head has a faint dark hood and the bill is thick, not especially long, and is all black except for a pale base of the mandible. While all of these characters seemed good for Slaty-backed Gull, the wing shape and primary pattern tends to make me think of something else, like maybe just a bulky male Herring Gull. P10 thru P6 are dark on the outside and pale on the inner web. P5 thru P1 are pale with a noticeable black terminal spot. The inner primaries are noticeably paler than the outer primaries and don't seem to have the expected tongue shape created by the white inner web, which would create the string of pearls. When folded, the tail seems to reach P7 in almost every photo. This character seems to be intermediate between Herring and Slaty-backed Gull. However in flight, the wings look more pointed and not as rounded as I would expect for Slaty-backed. The secondaries are all noticeably dark and are particularly darker than the coverts. The underside of the primaries is silvery pale. The tail appears to be completely dark with perhaps just a hint of pale coloration at the base of the outer retrices only.
